  ---
  Summary of docs/the-builder/

  This is a 5-session implementation plan for a Pokemon Team Builder feature вҖ” a
   competitive Pokemon workbench that integrates tools players currently use in
  isolation (Showdown builder, Pikalytics, VGC MultiCalc, etc.).

  context.md вҖ” Full Design Spec

  The definitive reference document covering 20 sections:
  - Vision: Replace 10+ fragmented tools with one integrated builder
  - Layout: Split-panel (editor 50% + context tabs 50%), inline species picker
  takes full width
  - Components: Team strip, EV editor with nature bump ticks, species picker
  with data table + detail panel, move/item/ability/nature/tera pickers
  - Context tabs: Types (defensive matrix), Speed (tier comparisons), Calc
  (damage calculator via @smogon/calc)
  - Meta pipeline: Schema for importing tournament data from Limitless, RK9,
  Showdown (tables created but empty in V1)
  - Validation: Three layers вҖ” strip badges, inline field errors, summary panel
  - Import/export: Showdown paste, Pokepaste URL, per-Pokemon paste

  Session Breakdown

  Session: S1: Foundations
  Focus: Data layer
  Model: Opus
  Key Deliverables: DB migration (7 new tables + column additions), package
    functions (calculateNatureBumps, getFormatSpeedBenchmarks, searchSpecies),
    team CRUD queries/mutations, Server Actions, @smogon/calc install
  в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җ

    sidebar nav. Track B: Editor workspace, team strip, pokemon editor, EV/IV

     рҹ“Ғ Files: `apps/web/src/app/api/e2e/seed/route.ts:130-136`

     рҹ”Қ Concern: The POST handler runs `checkBranchSafety()` and returns 
     diagnostic fields (`supabaseUrl`, `currentRef`, `productionRef`) in the 
     error response BEFORE validating the `x-e2e-seed-secret` header. An 
     unauthenticated caller on preview/dev can probe DB configuration.

     рҹҹЎ Validity: Valid вҖ” the route is already blocked on production 
     (`checkBranchSafety` rejects non-preview/dev environments), so the risk is 
     limited to preview deployments. But it's still a minor info leak вҖ” no 
     reason to expose refs before auth.

     рҹ’Ў Recommended fix: Move the secret validation (lines 138-144) above the 
     `checkBranchSafety()` call, so unauthenticated callers get a 401 before 
     seeing any diagnostics. Which approach? вҶ’ Move secret check first 
     (Recommended)

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:

      16 +  const requestHeaders = await headers();

         +bypass");

         +cret) {                                                        
      21 +    return;

      23 +

      25    if (isBot) throw new Error("Access denied");
      26  }

вҸә I see the issue. When the JWT is "nodots" (no dots), split(".")[1] is
  undefined, so the if (payload) guard at line 71 is falsy. The code falls
  through to the end of the try block without calling setHasAccess(false) вҖ” it
  only gets setIsLoading(false) from the finally block. hasAccess stays at its
  initial false default but setHasAccess is never explicitly called.

  The test expects mockSetHasAccess to be called with false, but the hook just
  doesn't call it in this path. The test expectation is wrong вҖ” the hook relies
  on the initial state being false. Let me fix the test:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

   (since the initial state is already false):

вҸә User approved Claude's plan
  вҺҝ В Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/calm-cooking-bengio.md В· /plan to edit
     Fix: Replace JWT-based team builder access check with direct DB query

     Context

     The team builder pages gate access via a team_builder_access JWT claim set
     by a Supabase custom_access_token_hook. This approach is broken in local
     dev вҖ” the JWT in the cookie is stale (issued before the hook migration was
     applied), and local Supabase Auth doesn't reliably invoke the hook even
     after re-login. The result: 404 on all team builder pages despite the
     feature flag being enabled and the user having site_admin role.

     The fix: query the database directly for server-side feature gating. JWT
     claims are appropriate for client components (avoiding round-trips), but
     every team builder page is a Server Component that already hits the
     database.

     Implementation

     1. Add hasTeamBuilderAccess() to 
     packages/supabase/src/queries/feature-flags.ts

     Reuse existing helpers: getFeatureFlag() (same file) + isSiteAdmin() (from
     site-roles.ts). Run both in parallel. Return true if any condition is met:
     - Flag globally enabled
     - User ID in metadata.allowed_users
     - User has site_admin role

     Fail-closed: catch errors, return false.

     2. Export from packages/supabase/src/queries/index.ts

     Add hasTeamBuilderAccess to the feature flags export block.

     3. Update 3 team builder server pages

     Replace the JWT decode block with a single DB query call in each:

     - apps/web/src/app/(dashboard)/dashboard/alts/[username]/teams/page.tsx
     - apps/web/src/app/(dashboard)/dashboard/alts/[username]/teams/new/page.tsx
     - apps/web/src/app/(dashboard)/dashboard/alts/[username]/teams/[teamId]/lay
     out.tsx

     Before:
     const { data: { session } } = await supabase.auth.getSession();
     const claims = session?.access_token
       ? decodeJwtClaims<{ team_builder_access?: boolean
     }>(session.access_token)
       : null;
     if (!claims?.team_builder_access) { notFound(); }

     After:
     const canAccess = await hasTeamBuilderAccess(supabase, user.id);
     if (!canAccess) { notFound(); }

     Remove decodeJwtClaims import from each, add hasTeamBuilderAccess to
     @trainers/supabase import.

     4. Update dashboard layout

     apps/web/src/app/(dashboard)/dashboard/layout.tsx вҖ” add
     hasTeamBuilderAccess(supabase, user.id) to the existing Promise.all (line
     34). Remove the JWT decode block (lines 159-176). Remove decodeJwtClaims
     import.

     5. Write tests

     Add tests to packages/supabase/src/queries/__tests__/feature-flags.test.ts:
     - Flag globally enabled вҶ’ true
     - User in allowed_users вҶ’ true
     - User is site_admin вҶ’ true
     - None of the above вҶ’ false
     - Flag row missing вҶ’ false
     - DB error вҶ’ false

     What stays unchanged

     - Client-side hook useTeamBuilderAccess (JWT-based, used by sidebar)
     - custom_access_token_hook SQL function (still needed for client-side)
     - decodeJwtClaims utility (still used by client code)

     Verification

     pnpm lint && pnpm typecheck && pnpm test
     pnpm dev:web  # Navigate to /dashboard/alts/admin_trainer/teams вҖ” should 
     load, not 404

      207      console.error("Failed to log flag_deleted to audit log:", 
           auditError);
      208    }
      209  }
      210 +                                                              
      211 +// ===========================================================
          +==================                                            
      212 +// Team Builder Access                                        
      213 +// ===========================================================
          +==================                                            
      214 +                                                              
      215 +/**                                                           
      216 + * Check whether a user has access to the team builder feature
          +.                                                             
      217 + *                                                            
      218 + * Access is granted when ANY of:                             
      219 + * 1. The `team_builder` feature flag is globally enabled     
      220 + * 2. The user's ID is in the flag's `metadata.allowed_users` 
          +array                                                         
      221 + * 3. The user has the `site_admin` role                      
      222 + *                                                            
      223 + * Fail-closed: returns `false` on errors or missing flag row.
      224 + */                                                           
      225 +export async function hasTeamBuilderAccess(                   
      226 +  supabase: TypedClient,                                      
      227 +  userId: string                                              
      228 +): Promise<boolean> {                                         
      229 +  try {                                                       
      230 +    const [flag, isAdmin] = await Promise.all([               
      231 +      getFeatureFlag(supabase, "team_builder"),               
      232 +      isSiteAdmin(supabase, userId),                          
      233 +    ]);                                                       
      234 +                                                              
      235 +    if (isAdmin) return true;                                 
      236 +    if (!flag) return false;                                  
      237 +    if (flag.enabled) return true;                            
      238 +                                                              
      239 +    // Check allowed_users in metadata                        
      240 +    const metadata = flag.metadata as { allowed_users?: string
          +[] } | null;                                                  
      241 +    if (metadata?.allowed_users?.includes(userId)) return true
          +;                                                             
      242 +                                                              
      243 +    return false;                                             
      244 +  } catch (error) {                                           
      245 +    console.error("[hasTeamBuilderAccess] Error checking acces
          +s:", error);                                                  
      246 +    return false;                                             
      247 +  }                                                           
      248 +}

вҸә The URL in the screenshot is /dashboard/alts/admin_trainer/teams вҖ” so the
  sidebar sent you to the alt-scoped page instead of /dashboard/teams. That
  means currentAltUsername is resolving to admin_trainer even though "All Alts"
  is selected.

  Let me check why:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

вҸә There's the bug. Line 621:

  const currentAltUsername = selectedAlt?.username ?? alts[0]?.username ?? null;

  When "All Alts" is selected, selectedAlt is null вҖ” but then it falls back to
  alts[0]?.username which gives admin_trainer. So currentAltUsername is never
  null as long as the user has any alts, which means it always takes the
  alt-scoped path.

  The fix: currentAltUsername should only be set when a specific alt is selected
   вҖ” not fall back to the first alt.

вң» Churned for 3m 12s

вқҜ does the type match up chart take into account the moves of all the pokemon   
  in the team?                                                                  

вҸә No вҖ” the type coverage matrix in the mockup only shows defensive matchups (how
   each type hits each of your Pokemon). It doesn't account for your team's
  offensive coverage (what types your moves can hit super-effectively).

  The current implementation in the codebase does have an offensive coverage
  section, but it's separate from the matrix.

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· How should offensive coverage integrate with the type matrix? The 
     defensive heatmap shows what hits your team вҖ” should offensive coverage be 
     part of the same view? вҶ’ Combined single matrix with both

вҸә Combined matrix вҖ” one view showing both defensive AND offensive for each cell.
   That's dense but powerful. Let me think about how to represent both pieces of
   info in one cell.

  The challenge: each cell currently shows one value (defensive multiplier). Now
   it needs to show two: "this type hits Pokemon X at 2Г—" AND "Pokemon X can hit
   this type at 2Г— with [move name]."

вҸәВ User answered Claude's questions:
  вҺҝ В В· For the combined matrix, each cell needs to show both defensive 
     (incoming) and offensive (outgoing) info. How should this look in a single 
     cell? вҶ’ i think we need toggles. because i want to be able to see how the 
     collective team does offensively in general against all types. and how the 
     team does collectively defensively. also i want to be able to scope down to
      a single pokemon

вҸә That's a much clearer mental model вҖ” toggles for different views rather than
  cramming everything into one cell. So the Types tab has:

  1. View toggle: Defensive / Offensive
  2. Scope toggle: Full Team / Selected Pokemon

  That gives you 4 combinations:
  - Defensive + Full Team: the heatmap we already have (all 6 Pokemon columns)
  - Defensive + Selected Pokemon: individual weaknesses/resistances for the
  selected Pokemon
  - Offensive + Full Team: what types your team can hit SE (based on all moves
  across all 6)
  - Offensive + Selected Pokemon: what types the selected Pokemon's 4 moves can
  hit SE

  Plus the insights/warnings section adapts to whichever view is active.

  This is getting more defined. I have enough to write this up. Anything else
  you want to explore before I write the design spec, or are we ready?
